});\r\n\r\n        // In Chrome, an anchor tag with target=\"_blank\" and a \"mailto:\" href opens a new tab/window as well as the email client\r\n        // I suspect this behavior will be corrected in the future\r\n        // Remove the target=\"_blank\"\r\n        $('ul.wi-affiliationList').find('a[href^=\"mailto:\"]').each(function () {\r\n            $(this).removeAttr('target');\r\n        });\r\n    });\r\n</script>\r\n\r\n \n    </div>\n    <div class=\"widget widget-ArticleLinks widget-instance-OUP_Article_Links_Widget\">\n         \n    </div>\n\r\n\r\n        <div <div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=92087139 id=\"92087139\" class=\"abstract-title\" >Abstract</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Optically bright, wide separation double (gravitationally lensed) quasars can be easily monitored, leading to light curves of great importance in determining the Hubble constant and other cosmological parameters, as well as the structure of active nuclei and haloes of galaxies. Searching for new double quasars in the Sloan Digital Sky Survey III (SDSS-III) data base, we discovered SDSS J1442+4055. This consists of two bright images (<em>r</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a018\u201319) of the same distant quasar at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.575. The two quasar images are separated by \u223c2<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\prime\\prime}_{.}}$|</span>1, show significant parallel flux variations and can be monitored from late 2015. We also found other two double quasar candidates, SDSS J1617+3827 (<em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.079) and SDSS J1642+3200 (<em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.264), displaying evidence for the presence of a lensing object and parallel flux variations, but requiring further spectroscopic observations to be confirmed as lensed quasars.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong \u2013 methods: data analysis&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong \u2013 methods: data analysis</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;methods: observational&quot;\">methods: observational</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;quasars: general&quot;\">quasars: general</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=92087141 id=\"92087141\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Variability studies of gravitationally lensed quasars (GLQs) are a powerful means to study the Universe (e.g. Schneider, Kochanek &amp; Wambsganss <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib43\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib43\" data-open=\"bib43\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>). For example, time delays of GLQs are used to estimate cosmological parameters, primarily the current expansion rate of the Universe (the so-called Hubble constant; Oguri <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib32\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib32\" data-open=\"bib32\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>; Suyu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib48\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib48\" data-open=\"bib48\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib49\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib49\" data-open=\"bib49\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Sereno &amp; Paraficz <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib44\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib44\" data-open=\"bib44\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Rathna Kumar, Stalin &amp; Prabhu <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib41\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib41\" data-open=\"bib41\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). In addition, microlensing-induced flux variations reveal, among other things, the structure of quasars and properties of populations of stars (microlenses) in galaxies (e.g. Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>; Eigenbrod et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Poindexter, Morgan &amp; Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib39\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib39\" data-open=\"bib39\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Dai et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Morgan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Hainline et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Mosquera et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Blackburne et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; MacLeod et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). Multiwavelength intrinsic variability of GLQ images also produces valuable reverberation maps of emitting regions of quasars (Gil-Merino et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Goicoechea et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), which will become critical tools to check microlensing-derived source structures.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">As searching for new lensed quasars and conducting subsequent monitoring campaigns are tasks of great relevance in cosmology, current quasar data bases are being deeply mined to discover new GLQs (e.g. Oguri et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib33\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib33\" data-open=\"bib33\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Inada et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Jackson et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Elyiv et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Buckley-Geer et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Agnello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015b</a>; Nord et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib31\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib31\" data-open=\"bib31\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), and several techniques are being developed to search for GLQs in ongoing and future surveys (e.g. Agnello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015a</a>; Chan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). The GLQ zoo includes rare phenomena consisting of two optically bright images (<em>r</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a020) of the same distant quasar that are separated by \u0394\u03b8\u00a0&gt;\u00a02\u00a0arcsec. Only 5 out of the 100 multiply imaged systems in the CfA-Arizona Space Telescope Lens Survey (CASTLES) data base<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\"><sup>1</sup></a> satisfy these conditions. Each of the optically bright, wide separation double quasars is of particular interest because it can be easily monitored with an 1\u20132\u00a0m class telescope in average seeing conditions, and the time delay between its two images can be obtained from light curves and cross-correlation techniques (e.g. Poindexter et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib38\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib38\" data-open=\"bib38\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>; Shalyapin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib47\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib47\" data-open=\"bib47\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Koptelova et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Eulaers et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Rathna Kumar et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>). Detection of time delays between different optical bands (e.g. Koptelova et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) and uncorrelated (microlensing-induced) variations in light curves of the quasar images (e.g. Oscoz et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib34\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib34\" data-open=\"bib34\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>) is also possible.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The ongoing monitoring projects do not only focus on bright and widely separated double quasars, although several targets belong to this type of systems. There are currently many cross-correlation techniques to determine time delays of GLQs (e.g. Liao et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), and the Cosmological Monitoring of Gravitational Lenses (COSMOGRAIL) is a collaboration targeting \u223c20 GLQs to (mainly) measure their time delays (Tewes et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib50\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib50\" data-open=\"bib50\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). The COSMOGRAIL website<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn2\" data-open=\"fn2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\"><sup>2</sup></a> incorporates a list of main publications, light curves and other relevant information. This large collaboration uses 1\u20132\u00a0m telescopes in both hemispheres, and has published light curves and time delays of 7 GLQs with optically bright images. Two of them are widely separated doubles (Eulaers et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Rathna Kumar et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>), three are quads with some widely-separated images, and two are doubles with \u0394\u03b8\u00a0\u223c\u00a01\u00a0arcsec. Other groups are also involved in similar programmes. For example, the Gravitational Lenses and Dark Matter (GLENDAMA) project is conducting an optical monitoring of \u223c10 bright GLQs with different angular sizes.<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn3\" data-open=\"fn3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\"><sup>3</sup></a> The GLENDAMA team uses a 2\u00a0m robotic telescope in the north hemisphere with the purpose of measuring time delays, and analysing intrinsic and extrinsic (microlensing) flux variations (e.g. Goicoechea, Shalyapin &amp; Ull\u00e1n <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In this paper, we present our ongoing search for GLQs in the Sloan Digital Sky Survey III (SDSS-III) data base (Eisenstein et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>). The selection of GLQ candidates and the corresponding identification campaigns are described in Section\u00a02. All candidates are composed of two point-like sources: one of them is a confirmed quasar and the other belongs to an unknown class. Our spectroscopic observations confirm the GLQ nature of SDSS J1442+4055, which has been independently discovered by More et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). In Section\u00a03, using new deep imaging in the <em>r</em> band, we present astro-photometric solutions and lens models for this optically bright, wide separation lens system. Our conclusions and future prospects appear in Section\u00a04.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=92087146 id=\"92087146\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>SELECTION AND IDENTIFICATION OF GLQ CANDIDATES</h2>\r\n                    <h3 scrollto-destination=92087147 id=\"92087147\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-1>Samples</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Our first sample (S1) of GLQ candidates is based on the SDSS-III Data Release 9 (Ahn et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). We used the Data Release 9 Quasar (DR9Q) catalogue containing 87 822 spectroscopically confirmed objects (Paris et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), as well as <em>gri</em> frames including these quasars and other surrounding sources. We initially checked for the presence of some point-like source in the vicinity (1\u20136\u00a0arcsec apart) of each DR9Q quasar over the redshift interval 0.8 &lt; <em>z</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a04 and brighter than <em>r</em>\u00a0=\u00a021. After finding an association, the similarity of colours of the quasar and its companion was probed. Specifically, we estimated the average magnitude difference, AMD\u00a0=\u00a0(\u0394<em>g</em> + \u0394<em>r</em> + \u0394<em>i</em>)/3 for each pair, and then selected pairs satisfying the constraints d<em>g</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a00.4, d<em>r</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a00.4 and d<em>i</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a00.4, where d<em>g</em>\u00a0=\u00a0\u0394<em>g</em> \u2212 AMD, d<em>r</em>\u00a0=\u00a0\u0394<em>r</em> \u2212 AMD and d<em>i</em>\u00a0=\u00a0\u0394<em>i</em> \u2212 AMD. After visual inspection of the selected targets, we obtained a sample of 39 candidates.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">To construct a second sample (S2), we used the SDSS-III DR10 (Ahn et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Paris et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>) and adopted a selection method different from the previous one (see above). We concentrated on quasars in the range RA\u00a0=\u00a0180\u00b0\u2013360\u00b0, over the redshift interval 1\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>z</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a05 and brighter than <em>r</em>\u00a0=\u00a020. We then searched for neighbour point-like sources at \u0394\u03b8 \u2264 6\u00a0arcsec. For the widely separated quasar-companion pairs (\u0394\u03b8\u00a0&gt;\u00a02\u00a0arcsec), a detailed colour test was also done. Using the corresponding <em>ugriz</em> frames, we compared colours of quasars and their companions, and selected pairs satisfying the constraints |\u0394(<em>u</em> \u2212 <em>g</em>)|\u00a0&lt;\u00a00.4, |\u0394(<em>g</em> \u2212 <em>r</em>)|\u00a0&lt;\u00a00.2, |\u0394(<em>r</em> \u2212 <em>i</em>)|\u00a0&lt;\u00a00.2 and |\u0394(<em>i</em> \u2212 <em>z</em>)|\u00a0&lt;\u00a00.4. After visual inspection, we selected 17 GLQ candidates for the S2 sample.<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn4\" data-open=\"fn4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\"><sup>4</sup></a> None of these new targets is included in S1.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Our selection criteria differ from those used to make the statistical lens sample of the SDSS Quasar Lens Search (SQLS; Oguri et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib33\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib33\" data-open=\"bib33\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Inada et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), since we focus on double quasar candidates with separations of a few arcseconds, which are within a larger cosmic volume and cover a wider range of magnitudes. However, the SQLS data base<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn5\" data-open=\"fn5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\"><sup>5</sup></a> also contains additional double quasars that are not included in the statistical sample (e.g. Inada et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>).</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=92087151 id=\"92087151\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-2>Follow-up observations of selected subsamples</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">From the whole S1 sample in Section\u00a02.1, we took a subsample (SS1) of three targets to perform follow-up observations (see Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>). We focused on \u223c10\u00a0per\u00a0cent of the initial sample in the RA interval 110\u00b0\u2013120\u00b0. These three SS1 candidates in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> have a large separation, and the immediate goal of the observations was to check the efficiency of our first selection method and try to discover some new GLQ. We attempted to obtain decent spectra for all SS1 targets in 2014. However, the spectra of the faintest candidate were very noisy, so it was also imaged. For this candidate, in Section\u00a02.3, we only present the analysis of its astro-photometric data.</p>                        <a id=\"92087153\" scrollto-destination=\"92087153\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Identification of GLQ candidates. J2053-0100\u00a0</td><td>2.207\u00a0</td><td>313.38756\u00a0</td><td>\u221201.01622\u00a0</td><td>1.43\u00a0</td><td>AZT-22/SNUCam (2015 Jun 17)\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td><td>Unlikely\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>SDSS J2153+2732\u00a0</td><td>2.216\u00a0</td><td>328.31784\u00a0</td><td>+27.54302\u00a0</td><td>3.62\u00a0</td><td>AZT-22/SNUCam (2015 Jun 20)\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td><td>Unlikely\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class=\"table-wrap-foot\"><span id=\"fn-TFN001\"></span><div content-id=\"TFN001\"><span class=\"fn\"><p class=\"chapter-para\"><em>Note.</em><sup>\u22c6</sup>Identified as a quasar+star system by More et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>).</p></span></div></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/92087153\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">We selected \u223c80\u00a0per\u00a0cent of the S2 sample, i.e. 14 out of the 17 initial candidates (see Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>), to make a second subsample in the RA interval 180\u00b0\u2013330\u00b0 (SS2). We first obtained follow-up images for 13 SS2 candidates at the Maidanak Astronomical Observatory (MAO) in 2015 June, and then attempted to conduct spectroscopic observations of each target whose follow-up images showed evidence for both a lensing galaxy and a variable companion. As almost all (12) SS2-MAO targets have a quasar at <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a02, the presence of a residual object (residual signal above the noise level) was considered as evidence for a lensing galaxy (see Section\u00a02.3). In addition, companion sources with flux variations (absolute differences between their SDSS and MAO magnitudes in the <em>r</em> band) of \u22650.1\u00a0mag were identified as variable objects. Unfortunately, we could not complete the spectroscopic observations due to observing constraints. However, we obtained spectra for the only SS2 target that was not imaged during the intensive observational campaign in 2015 June. This last candidate had weaker observing constraints than the pending targets showing flux variations and residual sources.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=92087155 id=\"92087155\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-3>Results</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">SDSS J0734+2733 is the brightest candidate, i.e. two components with <em>r</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a017. This was observed with the integral field spectrograph (FRODOSpec) on the 2\u00a0m Liverpool Telescope (LT). A 3200\u00a0s exposure on a dark night under normal seeing conditions was taken with this instrument. FRODOSpec is characterized by a field of view and a spatial scale of \u223c10\u00a0arcsec\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010\u00a0arcsec and 0<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\prime\\prime}_{.}}$|</span>8\u00a0pixel<sup>\u22121</sup>, respectively, and allows us to extract individual spectra for two point-like sources separated by a few pixels (Shalyapin &amp; Goicoechea <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). We also note that the spectrograph has two independent arms, allowing simultaneous spectroscopy at blue and red wavelengths. However, the sensitivity of its red arm is significantly higher, so we only show the red spectra of SDSS J0734+2733 in the left-hand panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>. The original FRODOSpec/red-arm data (spectral resolving power <em>R</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a02200) have been smoothed using a rectangular smoothing window of 24\u00a0\u00c5. While the confirmed quasar (component A, red line) shows a Mg\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> emission line near 8200\u00a0\u00c5, this feature is absent in the spectrum of its companion (component B, blue line). Hence, we conclude that SDSS J0734+2733 is not a double quasar.</p>                        <a id=\"92087157\" scrollto-destination=\"92087157\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/456/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2763/1/m_stv2763fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611467206&amp;Signature=ATCkmD3vFlHFcF-W~Azq7e4ugeHgexbig~tYKtJaZxUbevIsf6ct72H7yWy9bW1FT~jtRrwOrq67YN2cBgO50KKT9RhgU3296RVIoyq1C0nh8vstxAEDlORgOUwA5~qIrCLMm0gwu5gIgRfNoeF2gRDOO2tk4VkrDOlGbvWdbPg4qL5Gdjm1i2N6kV03fBldqmgNbxonpDEvp7z0XbNWTl5uhahU~KXhpqWUfP-YrCd0Jy3Un5WTANzGt6mnOU18Zls25LgpINNoU7rfdtMaTXn9Li~jP7ccvnwJq5R0odiUp3KjwHxjQuaWjuaLYkYyCCrd22Z76Db-BniyLa8BBw__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Follow-up observations of SS1 candidates. Here, B is the confirmed quasar and A its companion.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/456/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2763/1/m_stv2763fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611467206&amp;Signature=ATCkmD3vFlHFcF-W~Azq7e4ugeHgexbig~tYKtJaZxUbevIsf6ct72H7yWy9bW1FT~jtRrwOrq67YN2cBgO50KKT9RhgU3296RVIoyq1C0nh8vstxAEDlORgOUwA5~qIrCLMm0gwu5gIgRfNoeF2gRDOO2tk4VkrDOlGbvWdbPg4qL5Gdjm1i2N6kV03fBldqmgNbxonpDEvp7z0XbNWTl5uhahU~KXhpqWUfP-YrCd0Jy3Un5WTANzGt6mnOU18Zls25LgpINNoU7rfdtMaTXn9Li~jP7ccvnwJq5R0odiUp3KjwHxjQuaWjuaLYkYyCCrd22Z76Db-BniyLa8BBw__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Follow-up observations of SS1 candidates. Left and middle: spectra of the two components (A and B) of SDSS J0734+2733 and SDSS J0735+2036. In each panel, we also show the SDSS spectrum of the quasar (A) for comparison purposes. Right: I-band residual frame of SDSS J0755+1400. This is an inverted grey-scale image, so brighter sources correspond to darker zones. Here, B is the confirmed quasar and A its companion.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2763fig1.jpeg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/92087157/stv2763fig1.jpeg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2763fig1.jpeg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"92087157\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/456/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2763/1/stv2763fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611467206&Signature=PpmvBx~q5Ew54jug9X9d4~4oYjF8IlwNrMFj7n2vUmvLwurFX3ZGep3bnyh~6w5aKTnRGRCIDvdpvVnO8WHOkbGBzLE3d-sIUV~z0lwV3OwPm3zty9kcYsbM5nzGYoRdi~X3NZk0QwuMCSFh57YLTOrSIn1GVv4zWdtBE1J-mQv59uVD3fH9qcXvju6LU~~7mW8SVUC0IrU6ptDzgc7CwNVBW5-rWMntozUeAxfWsBxgiQ3u~7SelR3WtvaGD8I1J-6o7DPG685ZWpNnUKNFyIKVEurqRhPUjgBK8Ktc3eWylXXJz9T6jD3FdM4LlH7SLjUmuiSXvugPdFeSO9pYvQ__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=92087157&ar=1068469&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2763fig1.jpeg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Follow-up observations of SS1 candidates. Left and middle: spectra of the two components (A and B) of SDSS J0734+2733 and SDSS J0735+2036. In each panel, we also show the SDSS spectrum of the quasar (A) for comparison purposes. Right: <em>I</em>-band residual frame of SDSS J0755+1400. This is an inverted grey-scale image, so brighter sources correspond to darker zones. Here, B is the confirmed quasar and A its companion.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">SDSS J0735+2036 was observed with the Device Optimized for the Low Resolution (DOLORES) on the 3.6\u00a0m Telescopio Nazionale Galileo (TNG). We used the LR-B grism (<em>R</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a0600 and 0<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\prime\\prime}_{.}}$|</span>25\u00a0pixel<sup>\u22121</sup>) and the 1<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\prime\\prime}_{.}}$|</span>5 long slit, putting this slit in the direction joining both optically bright components (<em>r</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a019). The spectroscopic exposure of 1200\u00a0s was done on a dark night. In the middle panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>, we depict the TNG/DOLORES spectra of the quasar (component A, red line) and the previously unidentified object (component B, blue line). The continuum of B is similar to that of the quasar, but there are no emission lines superimposed. Thus, the companion object is likely a star.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Regarding SDSS J0755+1400 (<em>r</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a019\u201320), we obtained <em>I</em>-band exposures with the Andalucia Faint Object Spectrograph and Camera (ALFOSC) on the 2.5\u00a0m Nordic Optical Telescope (NOT). This camera has a spatial scale of 0<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\prime\\prime}_{.}}$|</span>19\u00a0pixel<sup>\u22121</sup>, which makes it a suitable instrument, in good seeing conditions, to try to detect a possible lensing galaxy between the two sources. Unfortunately, only half of individual frames were useful, and these were combined to produce a single deep exposure (1800\u00a0s of dark time under good seeing conditions). We then subtracted two point-spread functions (PSFs) from the NOT/ALFOSC combined frame of the candidate, using nearby stars as PSF templates. In the right-hand panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>, we display the residual frame after subtracting the two point-like sources centred at the green crosses. Actually the residual signal was smoothed with a median filter in circular neighbourhoods (4-pixel radius), and contains a possible very faint source (<em>I</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a022) close to the quasar B. However, this source (if real) is not expected to be the lensing galaxy of a quasar at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.845 because so faint lensing objects are usually associated with GLQs at <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a03 (see the CASTLES data base<sup>1</sup>). Assuming an early-type lens galaxy, we can also infer the expected value of the lens magnitude in the <em>I</em>-band as a function of the lens redshift <em>z</em><sub>lens</sub> (e.g. Rusin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>). The NOT/ALFOSC data are against the GLQ nature of SDSS J0755+1400, since the lens galaxy should have <em>I</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a019 at <em>z</em><sub>lens</sub> \u2264 0.8.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Using the Seoul National University Camera (SNUCam) on the 1.5\u00a0m AZT-22 Telescope (0<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\prime\\prime}_{.}}$|</span>27\u00a0pixel<sup>\u22121</sup>) at the MAO, we obtained 3600\u00a0s (6\u00d7600\u00a0s) exposures in the SDSS <em>r</em> and/or <em>i</em> bands for 13 out of the 14 SS2 candidates (see Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>). Most individual frames were taken under good seeing conditions [full-width at half-maximum (FWHM) \u2264 1\u00a0arcsec], and only three combined <em>r</em>-band frames led to residual signals above the noise level, i.e. residual sources with <em>r</em> \u2264 23. These combined frames are shown in the left-hand panels of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>. After subtracting two PSFs within the regions containing quasar-companion (A-B) pairs, the residual frames are also presented in the right-hand panels of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>. We only focused on the three targets having an associated residual source (R), which was interpreted as evidence of the existence of a lensing galaxy. The average redshift and separation for the 13 candidates are \u3008<em>z</em>\u3009\u00a0=\u00a02.3 and \u3008\u0394\u03b8\u3009\u00a0=\u00a02<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\prime\\prime}_{.}}$|</span>2, so there is a weak constraint <em>r</em> \u2264 23 on <em>r</em>-band magnitudes of possible early-type lens galaxies at <em>z</em><sub>lens</sub> \u2264 2. We also checked the variability of the companion sources (comparing their new MAO magnitudes with the corresponding SDSS data), since quasars are variable objects. This kind of test has been proposed by Kochanek et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>) and Buckley-Geer et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>) among others. The three companions are variable sources because we detected appreciable changes in their <em>r</em>-band magnitudes, i.e. |<em>r</em><sub>SDSS</sub> \u2212 <em>r</em><sub>MAO</sub>| \u2265 0.1.</p>                        <a id=\"92087161\" scrollto-destination=\"92087161\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig2\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/456/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2763/1/m_stv2763fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611467206&amp;Signature=qjpY8--PZ2qAPnpmlrZAoPgRxm14owjEc5ziPI5HSG8-7np9zq~dvQv8fE~GisfGuzDEIBoS3Py-UIw0GTZqGNLGO~wPHqkk5YHFHEtPwoY4Y29YIGeNe4AStXU3Vsi4oSjvsj0wOAOAcDvNmo57ryHlmIx8HQbPSjhRhu5vuLundSdg30BUYJ18bTbsS5sr1VUPSe1Qu7xy~u7tNok-u6Zr4ZXdiPwyDgTONVcHpzHDqndgmgLev789nEjQsdXt0w~stQFPYDNpzVn2uy2goCp03BlCuAGJd99~bz13QU~PPAr5jbdYYtOsbWNKJtPjXTo-rCpe8AHqF6auHEbRNg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"MAO r-band observations of three SS2 candidates. Left: combined 3600\u00a0s exposures of the quasar-companion (A-B) pairs. Right: residual frames. Each frame includes one residual object (R).\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2763fig2.jpeg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/92087161/stv2763fig2.jpeg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2763fig2.jpeg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"92087161\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/456/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2763/1/stv2763fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611467206&Signature=Qy6tDAljRah0D56GeByiwrcjoOPqs-nPaNbOfjrAqj3A-yal8SATXwOkBoG06-K92YIGNoPEwNwVcNCEV2dLXnCB~Et9DwKCM5ULu-8KJ8~B69JUTGROPuv1yIc72PVmhECDHQt5aZjC1pNHnyXXt5FZV7qvfpmyhcfi52Njlgba3yfAOQytp~-FqcYIEAHFbHkF~xCWnqc7G6sMrIOuzhZL2e38VDlpdOmZ9uqmWaYWeFE53PrSRbTHNGlXm-bc8pSaf8fY9AnOjekEJ-B0pD693zwKC9BN7XMg9NvIiQFw8rZgIzvo~GpTAZWRlSZ1kiFFxKtwZQQpAxOjMyPSfg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=92087161&ar=1068469&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2763fig2.jpeg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">MAO <em>r</em>-band observations of three SS2 candidates. Left: combined 3600\u00a0s exposures of the quasar-companion (A-B) pairs. Right: residual frames. Each frame includes one residual object (R).</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig2\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/456/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2763/1/m_stv2763fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611467206&amp;Signature=qjpY8--PZ2qAPnpmlrZAoPgRxm14owjEc5ziPI5HSG8-7np9zq~dvQv8fE~GisfGuzDEIBoS3Py-UIw0GTZqGNLGO~wPHqkk5YHFHEtPwoY4Y29YIGeNe4AStXU3Vsi4oSjvsj0wOAOAcDvNmo57ryHlmIx8HQbPSjhRhu5vuLundSdg30BUYJ18bTbsS5sr1VUPSe1Qu7xy~u7tNok-u6Zr4ZXdiPwyDgTONVcHpzHDqndgmgLev789nEjQsdXt0w~stQFPYDNpzVn2uy2goCp03BlCuAGJd99~bz13QU~PPAr5jbdYYtOsbWNKJtPjXTo-rCpe8AHqF6auHEbRNg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"MAO r-band observations of three SS2 candidates. Left: combined 3600\u00a0s exposures of the quasar-companion (A-B) pairs. Right: residual frames. Each frame includes one residual object (R).\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2763fig2.jpeg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/92087161/stv2763fig2.jpeg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2763fig2.jpeg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"92087161\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/456/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2763/1/stv2763fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611467206&Signature=Qy6tDAljRah0D56GeByiwrcjoOPqs-nPaNbOfjrAqj3A-yal8SATXwOkBoG06-K92YIGNoPEwNwVcNCEV2dLXnCB~Et9DwKCM5ULu-8KJ8~B69JUTGROPuv1yIc72PVmhECDHQt5aZjC1pNHnyXXt5FZV7qvfpmyhcfi52Njlgba3yfAOQytp~-FqcYIEAHFbHkF~xCWnqc7G6sMrIOuzhZL2e38VDlpdOmZ9uqmWaYWeFE53PrSRbTHNGlXm-bc8pSaf8fY9AnOjekEJ-B0pD693zwKC9BN7XMg9NvIiQFw8rZgIzvo~GpTAZWRlSZ1kiFFxKtwZQQpAxOjMyPSfg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=92087161&ar=1068469&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2763fig2.jpeg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">MAO <em>r</em>-band observations of three SS2 candidates. Left: combined 3600\u00a0s exposures of the quasar-companion (A-B) pairs. Right: residual frames. Each frame includes one residual object (R).</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">SDSS J1442+4055 has two bright components (<em>r</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a018\u201319), and the residual object appears in the expected position for a main lensing galaxy. A possible secondary lens also lies southwest of this object in the top-right panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>. Through PSF photometry in the <em>r</em> band (using standard <span class=\"small-caps\">iraf</span><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn6\" data-open=\"fn6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\"><sup>6</sup></a> tasks), we calculated magnitude differences between two epochs separated by \u223c10\u00a0years: SDSS (2003 March) \u2013 MAO (2015 June). For field stars, these differences were only about\u00a0\u00b10.01, while we obtained highly significant flux decrements of \u223c0.1\u20130.2 mag for both components. These are strong arguments in favour of the GLQ nature of SDSS J1442+4055, and thus, we selected this target for spectroscopic follow-up observations with the highest priority. The other two candidates: SDSS J1617+3827 (<em>r</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a019\u201321) and SDSS J1642+3200 (<em>r</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a018\u201321), do not show significant residues on the lines joining their components (see the middle and bottom-right panels of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>). The residual objects are located northeast of the bright quasar with <em>r</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a019 (SDSS J1617+3827) or around the faint companion object with <em>r</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a020 (SDSS J1642+3200). Additionally, the quasars and their companions have experienced flux decrements that exceed the noise level (0.01\u00a0mag) in factors from 3 to 30. Therefore, these two candidates also deserve more attention, and they were selected as secondary targets for spectroscopy. Unfortunately, we were not able to get decent spectra for both targets.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We observed SDSS J1442+4055 with the Spectrograph for the Rapid Acquisition of Transients (SPRAT) on the 2\u00a0m LT. Although the sky was relatively bright, the strong evidence for a GLQ and the near end of the target visibility window justified urgent spectroscopic observations. Using the blue grating and the 1<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\prime\\prime}_{.}}$|</span>8 long slit (<em>R</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a0350 and 0<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\prime\\prime}_{.}}$|</span>44\u00a0pixel<sup>\u22121</sup>), we took five 600\u00a0s exposures in normal seeing conditions (FWHM \u223c1<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\prime\\prime}_{.}}$|</span>3). The top panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a> shows the combined (3000\u00a0s) spectra of A (quasar) and B (companion source), which incorporate Ly\u03b1+N\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">v</span>, Si\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>+O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>], C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] emission lines at very similar wavelengths. A cross-correlation between the two spectra proved that their redshifts are identical,<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn7\" data-open=\"fn7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\"><sup>7</sup></a> and this corroborated the GLQ nature of SDSS J1442+4055.</p>                        <a id=\"92087164\" scrollto-destination=\"92087164\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/456/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2763/1/m_stv2763fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611467206&amp;Signature=xHiwhgorU8X6RwLkQRKCYQHW--ORfLGZCDwCn9wybcYpuEPpxToB3Av3Bg7hrBHz1wgznz4QG7NkN3x0MRFB~yisPyYA~3~Z-NIjp~mHhRFKyHIJba~0JUhr0tn-yYv5~FNFaxRECY1YTDJxqSuSDxwp7pn2IDg3NE5YL42vdQDJB5dyEIJqwfxT9FKQFZKIxZBjai6DP~S06Km7-plUbU~f7~3ohFb67FDk5aUUTvyMUrwPimM4b7crmwsTeGixkxFFBe6WAmwMhvsxGCAE0uzegM9PD2QI3ddG2y5hp~iR4xk7IGUtkoR2Hp-2yvGLfDADU9Agx5JwKin5GlOifg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"LT/SPRAT spectroscopic observations of two SS2 targets. We also show the SDSS spectrum of the quasar (B).\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2763fig3.jpeg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/92087164/stv2763fig3.jpeg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2763fig3.jpeg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"92087164\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/456/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2763/1/stv2763fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611467206&Signature=SSWTjfLtk-s2P01ivumw7fLFUkSDUqpMIqvBX~wBR~smv8y1IMHf5S4Fu~bIlCJDmkPck75JayeafEJ9EH7GcWwwE7KrUYD3q9hEjCEF1DHlbYBVlLXXV6oNuJP4gG3uoC1Xr~83mYBey0~55i-rO3o8hLSkj5I25GkeDFAU5JVYOnj8B-iDbOkZqsa4Y1QKX~Ju5i~zcfxxjpCWbWP1FwyjkkGqbOucU0T5AnPA~c7Fc8uAaPC3DMgCChxiGEXWFzOggQjY~0SS-HUQU90me3l0q5KKD4RlxTV-f0GsoMImJAUbcnkQrrVdxMhskJBsKTQY3P5fgv1MrMq~IJfUkg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=92087164&ar=1068469&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2763fig3.jpeg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">LT/SPRAT spectroscopic observations of two SS2 targets. Top: spectra of the two components (A and B) of SDSS J1442+4055. The SDSS spectrum of the quasar (A) is also displayed in this panel. Bottom: spectra of the two components (A and B) of SDSS J1655+1948. We also show the SDSS spectrum of the quasar (B).</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">We also obtained SPRAT spectra for the only SS2 target that was not observed at the MAO. The candidate SDSS J1655+1948 consists of a relatively faint quasar (B) with <em>r</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a020 and a bright companion (A) with <em>r</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a018, and its 3000\u00a0s spectra are depicted in the bottom panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>. For this GLQ candidate, the A component is a star whose spectrum incorporates several absorption lines at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a00. We failed again in a positive identification of a candidate selected by standard methods (see Section\u00a02.1), and this stresses the efficiency in detecting GLQs using more sophisticated selection criteria, i.e. existence of a residual object and variable components.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=92087166 id=\"92087166\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>SDSS J1442+4055</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The MAO <em>r</em>-band imaging of SDSS J1442+4055 (FWHM\u00a0\u223c\u00a01\u00a0arcsec) was also used to infer astro-photometric solutions for the new lens system. Through the <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> software (Peng et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib37\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib37\" data-open=\"bib37\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>), this was modelled as two PSFs (quasar images) plus a standard galaxy profile convolved with the PSF. We considered a 2D S\u00e9rsic profile (S\u00e9rsic <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib45\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib45\" data-open=\"bib45\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1963</a>) for the main lensing galaxy, since it can describe light distributions for different types of galaxies. In the left- and right-hand panels of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>, we display the residual signal after subtracting the two quasar images and the final residues after subtracting the global best fit (quasar images + main lensing galaxy), respectively. The main lens (G1) and the secondary lens (G2) are clearly resolved in the left-hand panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>. Apart from the solution leaving the concentration index (<em>n</em>) as a free parameter (S\u00e9rsic profile), we also used a de Vaucouleurs profile for G1 to obtain a second solution, i.e. fixing <em>n</em>\u00a0=\u00a04, rather than leaving it as a free parameter (see Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>). This is a reasonable profile for early-type galaxies and galactic bulges, and it may be useful for extracting quasar fluxes from optical frames in monitoring campaigns (e.g. Shalyapin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib47\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib47\" data-open=\"bib47\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>). However, the reduced chi-squared value is 1.8, so the 1\u03c3 confidence intervals that we give in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> should be taken with caution.</p>                        <a id=\"92087168\" scrollto-destination=\"92087168\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig4\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 4.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/456/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2763/1/m_stv2763fig4.jpeg?Expires=1611467206&amp;Signature=sw8Tp94UZLccBQiEHb~mZgG5DrWxPor60dEnE8xo7hi7z9oxIMk~j-8jJHu6EuFfUhSnkp-bURoSNShrYQw0ZH32-T1O2Ws8VhYoIpRBfe2-Rd0aLXErRbBIUU-Qud0mAC60yZHpq8LsLRT3fe4W86hxtiDPTwaR0GEQuYEil3m8fIV5L7Ha8qimcCHWiFXgyL7iwEWht6XVcIPUdupUEmyRF9vIShBX7NhuINFRNdPm-cUY49NgEjRsevuQC53Pr2d1fCngx2xNbd5bfETEgZO1TyFq65PaM1sT~3zTEWwPH8oZ6trganlceo~ZNjVAbJUi~bXKdQJ-A0FVKqOR0g__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"galfit model of SDSS J1442+4055 in the r band. This model includes three ingredients: two PSFs (quasar images) and the convolution of a 2D S\u00e9rsic profile with the PSF (main lensing galaxy G1). We show the residual signal after subtracting only the quasar images (left-hand panel) and after subtracting the global solution (right-hand panel).\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2763fig4.jpeg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/92087168/stv2763fig4.jpeg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2763fig4.jpeg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"92087168\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/456/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2763/1/stv2763fig4.jpeg?Expires=1611467206&Signature=CpKAEl8PpGJj-gTXGiNU1L8cXC2eG7OL6YVtfa2oHDAw7jssx5rsBqxW5~NyTe8Jru0vDSqQbElPBRJmiVyg6R7L95iHKyId~It1YDu5LcZPgmaPqECYiZYBdurUHlq4dSRmoHjSEhu5zFENqH5TKov1VuRWsnKKOsAkgo-OMLveXLjKkvU6q3OnAz9XDy3JfZjoKDMmvARXEc8yrQImDgUXAHVTv7OTRaeHeO8fvV4WHl8nR4uHozBvSYzqCSHtGolN92~WU3-dnnxOXtuJ51oJg9mkWGP9VOdq5pDHfEIYukZhqupWcVeua-wVHwH62p0-uXNY09XJdM82x43nIw__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=92087168&ar=1068469&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2763fig4.jpeg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\"><span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> model of SDSS J1442+4055 in the <em>r</em> band. <em>y</em><sub>G1</sub>), magnitude (<em>r</em><sub>G1</sub>), effective radius <em>r</em><sub>eff</sub>, ellipticity <em>e</em>, and position angle of the major axis \u03b8<sub><em>e</em></sub> (it is measured east of north).</p></div> </div><div class=\"table-overflow\"><table><thead><tr><th><em>x</em><sub>B</sub> (\u2032)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>y</em><sub>G1</sub> (\u2032)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>r</em><sub>G1</sub> (mag)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>r</em><sub>eff</sub> (\u2032)<span .\u00a0</span></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>2.096\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.003\u00a0</td><td>\u22120.506\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.001\u00a0</td><td>1.342\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.013\u00a0</td><td>\u22120.344\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.008\u00a0</td><td>19.47\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01\u00a0</td><td>0.59\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02\u00a0</td><td>0.19\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04\u00a0</td><td>\u221212\u00a0\u00b1\u00a06\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class=\"table-modal\"><table><thead><tr><th><em>x</em><sub>B</sub> (\u2032)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>y</em><sub>B</sub> (\u2032)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>x</em><sub>G1</sub> (\u2032)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>y</em><sub>G1</sub> (\u2032)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>r</em><sub>G1</sub> (mag)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>r</em><sub>eff</sub> (\u2032)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>e</em><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>\u03b8<sub><em>e</em></sub> (\u00b0)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>2.096\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.003\u00a0</td><td>\u22120.506\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.001\u00a0</td><td>1.342\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.013\u00a0</td><td>\u22120.344\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.008\u00a0</td><td>19.47\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01\u00a0</td><td>0.59\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02\u00a0</td><td>0.19\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04\u00a0</td><td>\u221212\u00a0\u00b1\u00a06\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/92087169\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">SDSS J1442+4055 has been independently discovered by More et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). When we were writing this report, More et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) announced the discovery of 13 GLQs, including SDSS J1442+4055 between their confirmed lens systems. They used a 900\u00a0s <em>i</em>-band exposure with the 2.4\u00a0m Hiltner Telescope to model the system, whereas our fits were based on an <em>r</em>-band combined frame with an equivalent exposure time (2.4\u00a0m telescope) of 1400\u00a0s. We note that our estimation of <em>r</em><sub>G1</sub> in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> coincides with the (<em>g</em><sub>G1</sub> + <em>i</em><sub>G1</sub>)/2 value from table 3 of More et\u00a0al. Although there is also agreement in the values of <em>e</em> and <em>r</em><sub>eff</sub> (the S\u00e9rsic profile led to <em>r</em><sub>eff</sub>\u00a0\u223c\u00a01\u00a0arcsec and a large index <em>n</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a04), our \u03b8<sub><em>e</em></sub> values are separated by \u223c90\u00b0 from the More at al.'s solution for the position angle.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Even though the redshift of the main lensing galaxy (G1) is still unknown, the current SDSS-MAO data give a hint as to the <em>z</em><sub>lens</sub> value. The SDSS spectrum of the A image shows the existence of an absorption system at <em>z</em><sub>abs</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.946, which was identified from 12 different absorption features in the wavelength range, 4500\u20138500\u00a0\u00c5. However, the Rusin et\u00a0al.'s scheme (Rusin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>) is in clear disagreement with a bright lens (<em>r</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a019.5, see Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>) at <em>z</em><sub>lens</sub>\u00a0\u223c\u00a02, so the distant absorption system is most likely not linked to G1. We may also consider a second scenario where G1 is physically associated with G2 (<em>r</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a020). As the SDSS data base includes a photometric redshift for G2 (0.32\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.05), <em>z</em><sub>lens</sub> would be \u223c0.3\u20130.4. This lens redshift is in good agreement with the MAO brightness of G1, and thus, the gravitational lens could consist of two galaxies at similar moderate values of <em>z</em>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We also modelled SDSS J1442+4055 using the relative astrometry in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> and the <em>i</em>-band flux ratio by More et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), as well as a singular isothermal sphere (SIS) mass model in a standard cosmology (e.g. Schneider et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib43\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib43\" data-open=\"bib43\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>). The <span class=\"small-caps\">lensmodel</span> software (Keeton <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>) led to a solution with \u03c7<sup>2</sup>\u00a0\u226b\u00a01, indicating we need to improve our model. The simplest option is to add ellipticity to the SIS mass distribution of G1. Thus, we used the <span class=\"small-caps\">lensmodel</span> package to find the singular isothermal ellipsoid (SIE) solution for the astro-photometric constraints. The number of model parameters was the same as the number of observational constraints, and the new solution was characterized by a mass scale <em>b</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a01<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\prime\\prime}_{.}}$|</span>08, an ellipticity <em>e</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a00.017, a mass orientation of about \u221260\u00b0 and \u03c7<sup>2</sup>\u00a0\u223c\u00a00. Although the ellipticity and orientation of the mass do not coincide with the ellipticity and orientation for the light distribution of G1 (see the two last columns in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>), we remark that we are dealing with an effective mass distribution, since the secondary lens (G2) was not modelled in any way. For this effective lens model (SIE), the expected time delay is \u223c40\u00a0d if <em>z</em><sub>lens</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.4 (A is leading).</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=92087173 id=\"92087173\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>CONCLUSIONS AND FUTURE WORK</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Using the SDSS-III DR9 (Ahn et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Paris et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) and DR10 (Ahn et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Paris et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>), we have searched for new double quasars with separations of 1\u20136\u00a0arcsec. As expected, samples of a few candidates selected from standard criteria (i.e. a quasar and a point-like companion source, having both similar colours) were largely inefficient tools to find new GLQs (e.g. Inada et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). For this reason, we introduced two additional ingredients in the selection procedure: presence of a residual source (lensing galaxy?) in a new deep exposure, and detection of flux variations by comparing the SDSS imaging and the new non-SDSS exposure.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">After an observational campaign at the MAO, we found three GLQ candidates satisfying all our selection criteria. The most promising target (SDSS J1442+4055) was spectroscopically observed in 2015 August, showing two identical spectra for the quasar and its companion (see also More et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). This is an optically bright, wide separation double quasar whose images appreciably vary in parallel on a 10-yr time-scale (see Section\u00a02.3). Therefore, SDSS J1442+4055 is an excellent target to be monitored with an 1\u20132\u00a0m class telescope from late 2015. Besides light curves of the two quasar images, new spectroscopy and deep imaging are required to accurately determine the lens redshift <em>z</em><sub>lens</sub> and the astro-photometric parameters. The current astro-photometric data suggest that <em>z</em><sub>lens</sub>\u00a0\u223c\u00a00.3\u20130.4, where the main lens would be the galaxy G1, while another neighbour galaxy (G2) would also contribute to the gravitational mirage. Spectroscopic observations of the other two GLQ candidates (SDSS J1617+3827 and SDSS J1642+3200) are also needed to determine their GLQ nature.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The new lens system SDSS J1442+4055 is now included in the GLENDAMA list of GLQs, so it will be observed with the LT, the 10.4\u00a0m Gran Telescopio Canarias and other facilities. We also plan to perform a spectroscopic follow-up of the two variable targets with residual sources (SDSS J1617+3827 and SDSS J1642+3200), as well as two additional variable targets that do not show residual sources with <em>r</em> \u2264 23 (SDSS J2053-0100 and SDSS J2153+2732, see Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>). In the near future, we will also explore the feasibility to find new GLQs in the SDSS-III and other data bases, by using pairs of unidentified point-like sources showing evidence for variability (e.g. Kochanek et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Buckley-Geer et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We wish to thank the anonymous referee and Anupreeta More for useful suggestions and comments that have helped to improve the original manuscript. The observations at the MAO were supported by the ISON project. We thank Seoul National University for equipping the AZT-22 Telescope with a modern CCD camera. This report is also based on observations made with the LT (Programme XCL04BL2), the Nordic Optical Telescope (Programme SST2014-057) and the TNG (Programme A28DDT8), operated on the island of La Palma by the Liverpool John Moores University (with financial support from the UK Science and Technology Facilities Council), the Nordic Optical Telescope Scientific Association and the Fundacin Galileo Galilei of the INAF (Istituto Nazionale di Astrofisica), respectively, in the Spanish Observatorio del Roque de los Muchachos of the Instituto de Astrof\u00edsica de Canarias. We thank the staff of all used telescopes for a kind interaction before, during and after the observations. We also used data taken from the SDSS-III web site (<a class=\"link link-uri openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://www.sdss3.org/\" target=\"_blank\">http://www.sdss3.org/</a>), and we are grateful to the SDSS-III collaboration for doing that public data base. This research has been supported by the Spanish Department of Research, Development and Innovation grant AYA2013-47744-C3-2-P (GLENDAMA project), and the University of Cantabria.</p><div content-id=\"fn1\"><span class=\"fn\"><span class=\"label fn-label\"><span rel=\"nofollow\" data-fn-id=\"fn1\" class=\"end-note-link\">1</span></span><div class=\"footnote-content\"><p class=\"footnote-compatibility\"><a class=\"link link-uri openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"https://www.cfa.harvard.edu/castles/\" target=\"_blank\">https://www.cfa.harvard.edu/castles/</a> (C.S. Kochanek, E.E. Falco, C. Impey, J. Lehar, B. McLeod, H.-W. Rix)</p></div></span></div><div content-id=\"fn2\"><span class=\"fn\"><span class=\"label fn-label\"><span rel=\"nofollow\" data-fn-id=\"fn2\" class=\"end-note-link\">2</span></span><div achieve a reasonable balance between compact (\u0394\u03b8\u00a0\u223c\u00a01\u20132\u00a0arcsec) and wide separation candidates, we did not consider targets with class=\"navbar-menu\">\r\n\r\n        </nav>\r\n            <div class=\"navbar-search-container js-navbar-search-container\">\r\n                <a href=\"javascript:;\" class=\"navbar-search-close       </select>\r\n\r\n                            <label for=\"MicrositeSearchTerm\" class=\"screenreader-text\">search input</label>\r\n                            <input class=\"navbar-search-input
